Mark Perez
Actually, it is science. I came from a background in science and nutrition. I realized that there was a variable (or two) that I hadn't accounted for, sunlight being one of them. Parts of our mitochondrion can run off sunlight, similar to plants. The mitochondrion was actually an invasive organism long ago in our system that became a symbiotic relationship forming the ADP->ATP cycle, but it can also use sunlight. (science has not told us the truth on this) Like Dr. Jubb, I have run for extended periods without any food, only tea and a bit of honey, gathering sunlight as energy, plus meditation. In the winter, I could not subsist only on sunlight because of where I live. I only needed to eat about 1/2 of my palm full of berries, and that was it, plus the sunlight, yoga, and meditation. I learned that when cleaned out, my skin became so absorbent that it pulled in water from the air, including nitrogen, and was able to actually form amino acids that, in school, I'd been told were impossible to do so because they required essential amino acids and could come from food only. (not true as I explored fasting) This isn't for everyone and should not be forced. I 'knew' and basically got a message along each part of the journey when I could live on various things... vegetarian, pescatarian, vegan, and eventually just fruits. Then I knew when I could do breathatarian. Do I live entirely without food now? No. I can though if I wish to and my system is completely detoxed/cleaned out. If someone forces this, it goes badly. I will also add that food is sometimes used by some in their spiritual journey to stay anchored and not leave their physical vessels turning into light bodies and wrapping up. This began to happen to me, and I realized that food (even meat) has the purpose of balancing us as we need to. Folks operating in lower frequency ranges are sustained by lower frequency foods better. Higher vibrations with higher vibrating foods, BUT I've also met some vegans and others that were way ungrounded and out of balance (top heavy in their chakras and energy systems) and needed to set vegan or higher vibration foods down for a bit to even things out. Sometimes folks are comfort eating/addiction eating. Sometimes people are eating foods to sustain themselves (which most of us need very little to do so actually). Sometimes those higher in vibration are eating food to stay anchored and not wrap up. To each their own and your mileage can and will vary. There is no rush. Don't force things.

Accountability For Health Industry Predators




Establish simple legal structures that define Health Industry Predation and hold perpetrators to account. 

Current examples are: 

* end of life care exploitation
* mandated medical experimentation
* coerced "well visits" where parents are threatened with the loss of their children 
* inappropriate diagnoses that lead to the use of inappropriate medications
* etc.

Instead of fining industries, the new laws would hold individuals to account along the entire production, marketing, and distribution chains practiced by Health Industry Predators. 

Health Industry Predation would be categorized as a type of organized criminal activity. 

When individuals and companies are charged and found guilty of Health Industry Predation, their businesses are shut down and their assets are seized. The foreseeable outcome of such a program would be billions if not trillions of dollars in cash on hand and assets being made available to build a HealthCare system that does not profit from predation.

Teach While You Sleep
It sounds like you're looking for someone to 'publish' your offerÂ Dainis. This is a super common thing where a marketer will take an expert (in this case, you) and run all their marketing and the expert will deliver any products and typically run a higher-ticket coaching program on the back end. Profit splits vary, but it's pretty common for the marketer to keep the front end profit (or loss since the marketer is typically the one putting up the cash to run ads to cold traffic) and there'll be a split of the back end coaching program. I know people who make a living publishing other peopleâ€™s offers.
However, with your offer in its current state, you may find it difficult - maybe impossible - to find an experienced marketer willing to publish you. The reason I say that is because it's not 100% clear what your product does (the outcome a student will get from it) or who the product is for. At the moment, the messaging is about your method, not the students' outcome.
The sales page talks about being for 'professional music teachers', but also for people 'just starting out'. No single person reading the sales page will have a â€œOh shit - this is EXACTLY what I needâ€ kind of response because no single person is simultaneously a professional music teacher, but also just starting out.
The outcomes it promises look like they're quite far-ranging as well - from sight-singing to songwriting to improvising on instruments to more general music literacy. Thatâ€™s not to say that your method canâ€™t help people with all these things, but talking about ALL of them means the messaging gets very diluted.
For example, you also mention that the method is 'amazing' for guitar, but I'm still not 100% sure what outcome a guitarist will get from the core offer. That variation you shared about writing your songs down is clearer, but honestly, that doesn't seem like a problem that millions of people have - which is what you need for the kind of scale you talk about. It seems like a very specific problem that very few people have - which means needing to charge high prices, but this problem doesn't really seem like something that commands a high price. Most singer-songwriters donâ€™t ever need to do this; they would usually just write the lyrics and chords down and can just record the melody demo as a voice memo on their phone. And if youâ€™re talking about guitarists specifically, the thing that will likely go through their minds is "I can just use tablature to write down songs."
Another reason it might be tricky to find someone to publish you is that you also mention a $7 CPA, but if you're talking about running cold Facebook ads, that's unrealistically low; especially if you want to scale. Your CPAs will go up after you've addressed the most eager buyers in the market and with the total value of your funnel at the moment - even with a $97 upsell - the economics of running this at scale just don't work out. If you had a high ticket coaching program on the back end that cost thousands of dollars, then that would be a different story, but I donâ€™t know what that would look like in your case.
You also mention your credentials and awards, but honestly, people don't care about that stuff; they care about what you can do for THEM. I also have degrees, but I almost NEVER mention them in my bass guitar business because it doesn't matter at all to the people watching my videos and going through my courses.
If you wanted this to be appealing to a marketer to publish, then Iâ€™d recommend making the messaging less confusing; less about your method and more about the outcome that a single type of student would get from learning what you teach. Try to make the core audience for the offer more on the beginner side (since mathematically, there will always be more beginners, and therefore, more potential to scale), make the total addressable market as large as possible, and increase the total value of the funnel so that there IS room to scale when CPAs rise to $50-$100+ if you start to seriously scale.
Also, marketers who publish experts will also usually prefer working with people who already have at least some kind of established audience as well - I'm not sure if that's something you already have, but if so, it would be appealing to a publisher.
All in all, this would likely be a hard sell to an experienced marketer, but from what you've written, it sounds like thatâ€™s what you want.

	â€¢	define: Displays the meaning of a word in a card-like result.

	â€¢	site:Â Limit results to a specific website.

	â€¢	intitle:Â Find pages that contain a specific word in the title.
	â€¢	allintitle:Â Like â€œintitle,â€ this finds web pages containing all of the specific words in the page title.
	â€¢	inurl:Â Finds pages with a certain word in the URL.
	â€¢	allinurl:Â Similar to â€œinurl,â€ this finds web pages containing all of the URLâ€™s specific words.
	â€¢	intext:Â Finds pages containing a specific word in the content.

	â€¢	AROUND(X)Â This proximity search finds pages containing two words (or phrases) within X words of each other.

Sculpture "Teleport", monument to Grand Duke of Courland Jacob Kettler in central KuldÄ«ga (Goldingen) in western Latvia. October 27, 2023

The sculpture ("Teleport") was created in 2013 by sculptor GÄ¼ebs PanteÄ¼ejevs and architect Andris Veidemanis. The object has two sides, symbolically revealing different eras. The front side, made of polished aluminium castings, symbolises the 21st century, while the back side is meant to be 17th century, made of rusted cast iron.
The object, which is more than two metres high, depicts Duke Jacob coming from the past into the 21st century. The site was chosen for its symbolic significance, as it is here that LiepÄja Street marks the end of the Old Town and the beginning of the new part of KuldÄ«ga. The object has two sides, each representing a different time period. The rusted cast-iron casting facing the Old Town symbolises the time of the Duchy, while the one facing the Town Square is a futuristic aluminium casting, from which Jacob emerges in the 21st century.
The greatest Duke of the Duchy of Courland and Semigallia reigned from 1642 to 1682. Under the Grand Duke Jacob of the Kettler family, Courland reached the highest stage of its development and power. Under his rule, shipbuilding developed rapidly, the first manufactories appeared and agricultural production improved. The Duke managed to create a large fleet, whose ships carried to Western Europe cereals, meat, butter, wool, timber and everything else produced by his manufactories and the manors of Zemgale and Kurzeme. The fleet was large and powerful, sailing not only to Europe, but also to Tobago and Gambia, establishing colonies there and taking sugar, coffee and spices to Europe.
The principality built ships, produced paper and napkins, wove cloth, brocade and tapestries. Ironworking was developed, nails were hammered, anchors and bells were made, guns were cast and firearms made, vodka was made, vinegar was produced and gunpowder was ground in mills. Sailcloth, cordage and hemp rope were also produced. The Duke also thought about seed breeding, raised pedigree livestock, improved the land with land reclamation... He contributed to economic and cultural prosperity, created manufactures, developed shipbuilding and industry, crafts and trade, founded colonies in Gambia and Tobago.

Sea Eagle II, built by Royal Huisman, is an 81-meter (266 feet) three-masted schooner and is currently the largest aluminum sailing yacht in the world. Designed by Dykstra Naval Architects and Mark Whiteley, this yacht features a narrow and efficient hull, a Panamax rig, and advanced engineering that includes the world's largest carbon rudder. The yacht's displacement at full load is 1,050 tons, and it is equipped with powerful winches capable of an 18-tonne pulling load.
The yacht's design emphasizes both performance and luxury, with a sleek plumb bow, spacious deck areas, and a refined interior. It accommodates up to 12 guests in luxurious settings and offers amenities such as a cinema room, gym, sauna, and a variety of water sports equipment. The yacht's owner, Dr. Samuel Yin, a Taiwanese billionaire, uses the yacht for both business and leisure, reflecting his preference for elegant, high-performance vessels.

 Fear of Your Parents' Old Age 

"There  is a break in the family history, where the ages accumulate and  overlap, and the natural order makes no sense: itâ€™s when the child  becomes the parent of their parent."
Itâ€™s when the father grows older and begins to move as if he were walking through fog. Slowly, slowly, imprecisely.
Itâ€™s when one of the parents who once held your hand firmly when you were little no longer wants to be alone.
Itâ€™s when the father, once strong and unbeatable, weakens and takes two breaths before rising from his seat.
Itâ€™s  when the father, who once commanded and ordered, now only sighs, only  groans, and searches for where the door and window areâ€”every hallway now  feels distant.
Itâ€™s when one of the parents, once willing and hardworking, struggles to dress themselves and forgets to take their medication.
And we, as their children, will do nothing but accept that we are responsible for that life.
The life that gave birth to us depends on our life to die in peace.
Every child is the parent of their parent's death. Perhaps the old age of a father or mother is, curiously, the final pregnancy.
Our last lesson. An opportunity to return the care and love they gave us for decades.
And  just as we adapted our homes to care for our babies, blocking power  outlets and setting up playpens, we will now rearrange the furniture for  our parents.
The first  transformation happens in the bathroom. We will be the parents of our  parents, the ones who now install a grab bar in the shower.
The grab bar is emblematic. The grab bar is symbolic. The grab bar inaugurates the "unsteadiness of the waters."
Because the shower, simple and refreshing, now becomes a storm for the old feet of our protectors.
We cannot leave them for even a moment.
The  home of someone who cares for their parents will have grab bars along  the walls. And our arms will extend in the form of railings.
Aging  is walking while holding onto objects; aging is even climbing stairs  without steps. We will be strangers in our own homes. We will observe  every detail with fear and unfamiliarity, with doubt and concern.
We will be architects, designers, frustrated engineers. How did we not foresee that our parents would get sick and need us?
We will regret the sofas, the statues, and the spiral staircase. We will regret all the obstacles and the carpet.
Happy  is the child who becomes the parent of their parent before their death,  and unfortunate is the child who only appears at the funeral and  doesn't say goodbye a little each day.
My friend *Joseph Klein accompanied his father until his final moments.
In  the hospital, the nurse was maneuvering to move him from the bed to the  stretcher, trying to change the sheets when Joe shouted from his seat:  Let me help you. He gathered his strength and, for the first time, took  his father into his arms. He placed his father's face against his chest.
He  cradled his father, consumed by cancer: small, wrinkled, fragile,  trembling. He held him for a long time, the time equivalent to his  childhood, the time equivalent to his adolescence, a long time, an  endless time. By Your Side Nothing Hurts
Rocking his father back and forth. Caressing his father. Calming his father. And he said softly:

 I'm here, I'm here, Dad! "What a father wants to hear at the end of his life is that his child is there."

it's is sooo racist to think that Haitian immigrants wouldn't practice their religion, culture, and folkloric traditions their way! 

Other cultures are different from ours. 

South Korea
In South Korea, cat meat was historically brewed into a tonic as a folk remedy for neuralgia and arthritis, not commonly as food. Modern consumption is seen and more likely to be in the form of cat soup, though the number of people who consume cat soup is considered minimal, compared to a relatively popular dog meat.

Julien Dugnoille wrote in The Conversation that cat meat is mostly consumed by middle-aged working-class women for perceived health benefits, and that usually 10 cats are needed to produce a small bottle of cat, or goyangi, soju (an alcoholic elixir thought to keep arthritis at bay for a few weeks at a time).

According to In Defense of Animals, 100,000 cats are killed yearly to make cat soju in South Korea. Cats are not farmed for their meat in the country, so the trade involves ferals and strays. Nonetheless, the trade is mostly done underground, and the great majority of the population is not even aware that cat consumption exists in the country. Moreover, eating cat meat is highly stigmatized throughout the country, unlike eating dog meat, which is often criticized but not universally stigmatized.

https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cat_meat

#Negritude, African Literature and Language Choice#
Expectations:
1. What is negritude? How did it come about?
2. What is African Literature? What gave rise to this variety of World literature?
3. Language debate in African Literature; which language should Africans use in expressing their experience and their literary works?
(1) Negritude:
Negritude is a  cultural, political and literary movement that began around 1930, spread through, 40s, and gain extrem popularity in the  â€™50s.
 At the out set, in the literary world, it began among French-speaking African and Caribbean writers living in Paris as a protest against French colonial rule and the policy of assimilation. Assimilation is a colonial policy, that aimed at transforming all Africans (particularly those in â€œFrenchâ€ colonies) by either luring or forcing them to integrate,  adapt and practice the way of life of the French people. It a policy that intended turning all Africans into black French men and women. To accomplish this goal, France had to eliminate all African cultures and assimilate all Africans into French culture. This policy never sat well with many Africans because it surpressed all the distinctive characteristics an Africans and this resulted to an intellectual protest.
 Negritude was majorly promoted by LÃ©opold SÃ©dar Senghor ( the first elected president of the Republic of Senegal in 1960) 
Some of the major principles of Negritude are: 
1. Celebration of Black culture and identity
2. Resistance to colonialism, racism, and oppression
3. Emphasis on the unique experiences and perspectives of Black people
4. Rejection of Eurocentric values and norms
5. Promotion of African and Caribbean cultures as equal to European cultures
In Literature, Negritude writers emphasized the following;
1. "Blackness" as a source of pride and strength
2. The importance of African and Caribbean heritage
3. The struggle for decolonization and independence
4. The role of literature and art in promoting social change
Major Contributors:
1. LÃ©opold SÃ©dar Senghor (Senegal)
2. AimÃ© CÃ©saire (Martinique)
3. Frantz Fanon (Martinique)
4. LÃ©on Gontran Damas (French Guiana)
5. Jacques Roumain (Haiti)
Negritude's legacy:
1. Inspired African and Caribbean writers to explore their cultural identities
2. Influenced the development of African literature and postcolonial studies
3. Contributed to the global fight against colonialism and racism
4. Shaped the Black Arts Movement in the United States
5. Continues to inspire contemporary debates on identity, culture, and social justice.
Conclusion:
Negritude's impact extends beyond literature to art, music, and politics, making it a significant cultural and intellectual movement of the 20th century.
To be continued

In Ancient Greece, Socrates had a great reputation for wisdom. One day, someone came to find the great philosopher and said to him:
"Do you know what I just heard about your friend?"
"A moment," replied Socrates. "Before you tell me, I would like to test it with the three sieves."
"The three sieves?"
"Yes," continued Socrates. "Before you speak about others, it's important to take the time to filter what you mean. I call it the test of the three sieves. The first sieve is TRUTH. Have you checked if what you're going to tell me is true?"
"No, I just heard it."
"Very well! So, you don't know if it's true. Let's move on to the second sieve, that of KINDNESS. Is what you want to tell me about my friend something good?"
"Oh, no! On the contrary."
"So," questioned Socrates, "you want to tell me something negative about him, and you're not even sure it's true? Perhaps you can still pass the test of the third sieve, that of UTILITY. Is it useful for me to know what you're going to tell me about this friend?"
"No, not really."
"Therefore," concluded Socrates, "what you were going to tell me is neither true, nor good, nor useful. Why, then, did you want to tell me this?"
"Gossip is a bad thing. Initially, it may seem enjoyable and fun, but ultimately, it fills our hearts with bitterness and poisons us." - Pope Francis

June 21st, 2015:
Not everyone you meet will give you the respect or love that you deserve. Respect them anyway. Love them anyway. No matter what you do, be kind. It is better to be kind and hurt, than unkind and cause pain. You were given the gift of gentleness and kindness. You were given the gift of a soft heart. So do not lose it. Do not allow your heart to harden. Just because someone caused you pain, it does not mean that everyone will. Just because someone betrayed your trust, it does not mean that others aren't trustworthy. Just because someone broke your heart, it does not mean that it will remain broken forever. It is better to love with a whole heart, to give with a whole heart, and to trust with a whole heart, than to never experience the beauty of love, the reward of giving, and the comfort of trusting. And when you fall hard, you can choose to remain on the ground for as long as you want, but you can also choose to get back up. Love again. Give again. Trust again. It is the experience that grows you, not the fear of it.

TRIGGER WARNING: reference to abuse.
Hi everyone, I've been sitting with this post for a while trying to find the right way to express myself. Let it be known that I'm trying to keep this post with as much of a sense of inquiry and openness as possible, whilst at the same time sitting in my place as an elder within my community who takes my responsibility to, and for ethical practice very very seriously indeed.
So much is coming to light right now about behaviour that is out of alignment in our spiritual communities. At the weekend, I was out with two dear friends and we were discussing "bystander apathy" (in a different context), the example given being where a bunch of people might be sitting in a room seeing smoke coming under the door, but because nobody else is shouting "fire" everyone else presumes things are ok...until they are not! 
This is what I see happening in our communities when people work without adhering to very strict and integral codes of ethics ('because it's spiritual and we don't need them"), and without truly walking in alignment with their personal and professional values. 
Too many things are slipping through the net because we are afraid to call them out. Whilst I don't agree with cancel culture, I do feel it's very important that people do the inner work to heal their own gaps in awareness(yes I see the irony of being able to do work on what is in principle a n invisible gap!) and take responsibility in humility when they/we deviate from 'the path'.
When concerns are named and shared, this is what I often hear within our communities:
"Well there's always two sides to a story"
"I don't do drama so I'm not going getting involved"
"It doesn't affect me and I've got enough on my plate anyway"
"If it's real they should go to the police" (yeah right because they are always a 'safe' option!!)
For me, referring back to the example about bystander apathy given above, there is often no smoke without fire or rather no fire without smoke showing itself first! 
No-one wants to see their friends called to account, that's hard right, but if they are really your friends, why are we not doing that in the first place, or why are we not asking those hard questions? 
If more than one person comes forward with concerns about another person's ethics or safety, I pay attention. I will then make choices about whether or not I attend those events, use those spaces, or communicate with others about what I'm hearing, and that's not always an easy decision to make. BUT if I sit and do nothing, knowing these things, I am surely part of the problem? I have been blocked by a male friend recently who did not like being called out about stuff (which I did in private FYI not to shame them) and yet in spite of the many attempts to do that compassionately before things got to that point, the person did not want to 'hear' it. 
The other thing I hear in our communities is that these things should be taken into circles to be discussed, without any recognition of the fact that the person making the allegation may feel completely unsafe being in another person's or people's company who has for example been the abuser or who has violated their boundaries in some way. This would be like asking a person fleeing domestic violence to sit with their abuser and chat because "you'll be safe" in circle. No! You may well not be! We have no obligation to 'fix' our abusers with a 'willingness to talk' until we feel ready, which may be never! You are not a bad person  or a coward for wanting to keep yourself safe! 
Having lived through many abusive situations, I can also see the parts in myself that remained unhealed that allowed me not to observe or pay attention to red flags, or where I simply did not know how to get out of those situations once in them. Many abusers are really charming and have lots of friends who think they are great but don't know or see what's going on in the background. 
I honestly feel that we are living in times where all of this stuff is now coming to the light and if we are to truly "Walk in Beauty" (a Navajo/DinÃ© prayer) as a collective, we MUST not ignore, collude or threaten legal action within the same systems that create the problems!!!! 
How can we speak softly to these things but bring in a strong dose of tough love when it's required?
Many of us who speak out end up being the target of backlash and retaliation, so we need to strengthen our communities so that we have ways that we can address these issues, register concerns somehow and know that there is supportive place to help us navigate those kind of challenges.
Speaking out about injustice has been a huge part of my life's work, and sometimes I really wish I could turn a blind eye for an easy life but I can't, so I am always willing to bear the brunt of that if it means I can stand in my own integrity with it. I usually think "would my children be grateful I took this stand" (for the Seven Generations to come).
No more can we cover up, hide, keep silent, keep secrets, keep on perpetuating the sickness that comes from the pain of our own or other people's unintegrated trauma (which I do feel compassionately is at the root of much of the dark behaviour). No more can we allow those things to go unspoken or be fearful of being exiled from our communities. 
To those who deviate, most of us can genuinely feel the remorse of a person who knows that they did wrong and is committed to making amends. We need to do better! 
We need the Elders to show the way, model good practice and we need safe, strong, boundaried Elders to do that. 
May we find our way home to the light with every breath we take.
For All Our Relations


Dana Millar

How to attract love? 3 techniques you should know
I am going to share with you 3 techniques worth trying to open yourself up to love.
I use these techniques in my new course entitled "OPEN TO LOVE"
1. Let go.
Let go of all the relationships that ever were.
Forgive and be thankful for all the relationships you've had.
Make a list of the things you are grateful for that person.
Really take a few minutes, and instead of focusing on what was bad, toxic about that relationship, focus on what you learned.
How has your life and your perception of the world changed?
What traits did you develop in this relationship / what did you learn?
What can you thank this particular person for?
Focusing on what was right and forgiving what was wrong. You free yourself from old patterns that you can repeat unconsciously and thus open yourself to something new.
2. Love yourself.
Your sense of worth and knowing that you deserve a wonderful relationship is the foundation of everything.
If you believe that you are worthless/deserving of no one, unfortunately that will be your reality.
If you don't respect yourself, don't have standards, and don't know your own values, the relationships you find yourself in will reflect that. People feel your energy.
3. New standards: we create a relationship
A very important step is to create a new one.
We create a new vision of who we want in our reality.
You can write a letter with the characteristics you want this person to have.
I would recommend that you write down how you want to feel about this person. He wrote how this person must feel about you. This step is based on the emotions you would feel having this relationship.
By creating this letter, answer me questions like?
- How do you want to feel with this person?
- How do you want that person to feel about you?
- you can put the appearance of the person (if it is important to you - you can put that the person is tall, thin, muscular, etc.)
- What do you do in your free time?
- Where do you go on dates?
- Does this person live in the same city?
- What is your contact with this person's friends?
- What is your contact with the family of this person?
- Do you have common passions?
This step is to let your imagination fly, write how you want to feel.
A very important step is to let go.
Hide this list and try to forget about it.
Let it manifest. Letting go of the magic and letting the magic work.

I've started writing a childrens' story about a friendly fawn named Freddy. Growing up to be a sprightly buck, he was convinced that all we need -- is love. He loved eating sprouting spring flowers and convinced all of the birds to come home to unconditional love -- to all!

All of the birds chirped and cheered whenever they say Freddy prance by!

Then Freddy went to the riverside to spread the message of unconditional love to more animals. A really really really big crocodile came to the river bank, and listened intently as Freddy explained to him the benefits of opening your heart to reciprocal love and blissful joy. Freddy showed the crocodile a breathing exercise and the crocodile practiced breathing in all sadness, converting it to love in his heart, and exhaling gladness. 

The crocodile told Freddy how amazing the breathing exercises were and how light he felt in his soul -- Freddy said: wow, I can come with some of my friends tomorrow -- and you can bring your friends -- and we can all breathe together and bask in the joy of universal unconditional love. 

The crocodile said: "I thought you'd never ask."

That night, Freddy had vivid dreams of his message of unconditional love spreading all around the world, to all of the animals -- even to humans. 

With birds chirping and cheering, Freddy went with 10 of his friends to the riverside, and lo and behold, the crocodile had also brought 10 friends. 

The crocodiles asked Freddy and his friends to lean in close close to their noses, to see if they were breathing together, correctly. 

And then all 11 crocodiles simultaneously ate Freddy and all of his friends for lunch. 

The end.

One of the most liberating realizations you can have is that you are only responsible for your own actions, thoughts, and feelings. It's crucial to understand that other people's behavior, choices, and reactions are their responsibility, not yours. Learning to say, "That's on you," is a powerful way to set healthy boundaries and protect your own emotional well-being.
When someone behaves poorly or makes choices that negatively affect their life, it's easy to feel sympathy and even guilt, wondering if you could have done something differently. However, it's essential to remember that every individual is accountable for their own actions. You can offer support and guidance, but ultimately, they must choose their path and face the consequences of their decisions. By internalizing this, you empower yourself and others to take ownership of their lives.
Recognizing what belongs to you and what doesn't is a key aspect of maintaining your emotional health. Absorbing the pain and problems of others can be incredibly draining and can hinder your ability to focus on your own growth and happiness. It's important to develop a clear sense of boundaries, understanding where your responsibilities end and someone else's begin. This doesn't mean you stop caring or become indifferent; rather, it means you can offer empathy and support without losing yourself in the process.
When you stop absorbing others' pain and start recognizing what belongs to you, you create space for your own emotions and experiences. This allows you to better manage your own life, make healthier choices, and maintain a positive outlook. It also encourages others to take responsibility for their actions, fostering growth and maturity in them as well.
Learning to say, "That's on you," is a form of self-respect. It means valuing your own well-being enough to not let others' actions and emotions dictate your mental and emotional state. It empowers you to stand firm in your boundaries, ensuring that you are not unduly influenced or harmed by the behaviors and choices of others.
Moreover, this mindset promotes a healthier dynamic in relationships. It encourages open and honest communication, where each person takes responsibility for their part. This leads to more balanced and respectful interactions, where both parties can grow and thrive independently and together.
In essence, embracing the mantra, "That's on you," fosters personal accountability and emotional freedom. It allows you to live authentically, focusing on what you can control and letting go of what you cannot. This approach leads to a more peaceful, empowered, and fulfilling life, where you can support others without sacrificing your own well-being. So, stand firm in your boundaries, recognize what belongs to you, and let go of what doesn't. Your life will be richer and more rewarding for it.

Some facts about bamboo:
1.Fast Growth: Bamboo is the fastest-growing plant in the world. It has been recorded at growing 47.6 inches in 24 hours. Some species can even grow over a meter per day under optimal conditions. A new bamboo shoot reaches its full height in less than a year.
2. Oxygen Release: A grove of bamboo releases 35% more oxygen than any other tree out there.
3. Carbon Dioxide Absorption: Bamboo absorbs carbon dioxide at a rate of 17 tons per hectare every year. It can act as a valuable carbon sink given how fast the plant grows.
4. No Fertilizer Required: Bamboo doesnâ€™t need fertilizer to grow. It can self-mulch by dropping its leaves and use the nutrients to grow.
5. Drought Resistance: Bamboos are drought-tolerant plants. They can grow in the desert.
6. Wood Replacement: Bamboos can be harvested in 3-5 years compared to the 20-30 years of most softwood trees.
7. Building Material: Bamboo is incredibly strong and sturdy. It has been used as support for concrete as well as scaffolding, bridges, and houses.
8. Soil Stability: Bamboo has a wide network of underground roots and rhizomes that prevent soil erosion.
9. Natural Air Conditioner: Bamboo cools the air surrounding it by up to 8 degrees in the summer.
10. Invasiveness: Some species of bamboo, especially â€˜runningâ€™ bamboos, can be invasive due to their extensive root systems, which allow them to spread rapidly. However, not all species are invasive, and with proper management, the environmental impact can be minimized.
Text credit: Earth Unreal
Image credit: Organizer Bamboo Nursery

Charlie Chaplin once told a joke in front of an audience..!!
Everyone laughed
And he told it a second time, so only a few laughed.
When he told it for the third time, no one laughed.
Then he said beautiful words.
If you can't laugh and laugh at the same joke, why do you cry and cry at the same pain and sorrow?
So enjoy every moment of your life - Charlie Chaplin left a great legacy without saying a word or hurting anyone's feelings. We remember these phrases that touch the heart.
*** Nothing in this life is permanent, not even our Problems.
*** I love walking in the rain so no one can see my tears.
*** The day you waste the most in your life is the day you don't laugh.

React differentiates between a component and a regular DOM element based on capitalization. For example, making an `` component with a lowercase name wouldn't work:

function article() {
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>React</h1>
      <p>Component</p>
    </div>
  );
}

ReactDOM.render(<article />, document.getElementById("root"));
Trying to render this component would result in React rendering an`` HTML elementLinks to an external site.instead of the `` component.

Using an uppercase name for the function fixes this problem:

function Article() {
  return (
    <div>
      <h1>React</h1>
      <p>Component</p>
    </div>
  );
}

ReactDOM.render(<Article />, document.getElementById("root"));
